class=3D"post-area instapaper_body"> <div class=3D"post-title-line"> <h1 class=3D"instapaper_ignore"><a href=3D"https://blogs.lessth= andot.com/index.php/desktopdev/mstech/powershell-in-your-vb-net-1/" class= =3D"post-title">Powershell in your VB.Net application the better way</a></h= 1> <div class=3D"post-byline"> by=20 <a href=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot.com/author/christiaan-baes-chrissi= e1">Christiaan Baes (chrissie1)</a> on March 21, 2011 in category=20 <a href=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot.com/categories/microsoft-technolog= ies">Microsoft Technologies</a> </div> </div> <div class=3D"post-tagline"> <a href=3D"https://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=3Dhttps%3a%2f%2fblogs.l= essthandot.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpowershell-in-your-vb-ne= t-1%2f&text=3DPowershell%20in%20your%20VB.Net%20application%20the%20bet= ter%20way" class=3D"twitter-share-button-static" target=3D"_blank"><i></i><= span class=3D"label">Tweet</span></a> <a href=3D"https://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=3Dtrue&url=3D= https%3a%2f%2fblogs.lessthandot.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpow= ershell-in-your-vb-net-1%2f&title=3DPowershell%20in%20your%20VB.Net%20a= pplication%20the%20better%20way&source=3Dhttps%3a%2f%2fblogs.lessthando= t.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpowershell-in-your-vb-net-1%2f" t= arget=3D"_blank" title=3D"Share on LinkedIn" class=3D"svg-button"><img alt= =3D"Share on LinkedIn" src=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot.com/images/linkedin= .svg"></a> <a href=3D"https://www.reddit.com/submit?url=3Dhttps%3a%2f%2fblogs.less= thandot.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpowershell-in-your-vb-net-1= %2f&title=3DPowershell%20in%20your%20VB.Net%20application%20the%20bette= r%20way" target=3D"_blank" title=3D"Submit to Reddit" class=3D"svg-button">= <img alt=3D"Submit to Reddit" src=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot.com/images/r= eddit.svg"></a> <a href=3D"https://www.facebook.com/sharer/sharer.php?u=3Dhttps%3a%2f%2= fblogs.lessthandot.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpowershell-in-yo= ur-vb-net-1%2f&quote=3DPowershell%20in%20your%20VB.Net%20application%20= the%20better%20way" title=3D"Share on Facebook" target=3D"_blank" class=3D"= svg-button"><img alt=3D"Share on Facebook" src=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot= .com/images/facebook.svg"></a> <a href=3D"https://www.instapaper.com/hello2?url=3Dhttps%3a%2f%2fblogs.= lessthandot.com%2findex.php%2fdesktopdev%2fmstech%2fpowershell-in-your-vb-n= et-1%2f&title=3DPowershell%20in%20your%20VB.Net%20application%20the%20b= etter%20way" class=3D"instapaper_button">Instapaper</a> </div> <div class=3D"post-content"><p>In <a href=3D"https://blogs.lessthan= dot.com/index.php/DesktopDev/MSTech/powershell-in-your-vb-net">yesterdays b= logpost</a> I showed you how to add powershell to your VB.Net application t= he esay way.</p> <p>Today I will show you a better way to do this.</p> <p>You might have noticed in the previous version that the system was waiti= ng for your statement to finish before it showed anything on the screen, in= other words it was doing this in an synchronized way, this is how the powe= rconsole extension for Visual studio currently works. It would be better to= do this in an asyncronized manner, like the nuget console.</p> <p>It isn=92t all that hard to accomplish this but it need some extra code = an a diffent way of working. First of all you will need to use the Runspace= and pipelines powershell makes available for you.</p> <p>I refined my code a little So I can easily choose which one to run.</p> <p>Here is how the app looks.</p> <div class=3D"image_block"> <a href=3D"https://blogs.lessthandot.com/wp-content/uploads/users/chrissi= e1/gitconsole/gitconsole2.png?mtime=3D1300715749"><img alt=3D"" src=3D"http= s://blogs.lessthandot.com/wp-content/uploads/users/chrissie1/gitconsole/git= console2.png?mtime=3D1300715749" width=3D"684" height=3D"420"></a> </div> <p>I added a button to run sync and async . And a button with some sample c= ode you can run. In this version BTW write-host will not really work. But w= rite will so use that.</p> <p>To start with I made an interface so I could easily run one or the other= .</p> <p><code>vbnet Namespace PowerShell Public Interface IRun Sub Run(ByVal Command As String) Event OutputChanged(ByVal Result As String) Event RunFinished() End Interface End Namespace</code> Then I implemented then sync way.</p> <p>```vbnet Imports System.Text</p> <p>Namespace PowerShell Public Class RunSync Implements IRun</p> <pre><code> Public Sub Run(ByVal Command As String) Implements IRun.Run Dim _Result =3D New StringBuilder Dim Results =3D System.Management.Automation.PowerShell.Create.AddS= cript(Command).AddCommand("out-String").Invoke(Of String)() For Each Result In Results _Result.AppendLine(Result) Next RaiseEvent OutputChanged(_Result.ToString) RaiseEvent RunFinished() End Sub Public Event OutputChanged(ByVal Output As String) Implements IRun.Outp= utChanged Public Event RunFinished() Implements IRun.RunFinished End Class </code></pre> <p>End Namespace``` Which is pretty much the same as what we already had in out previous exampl= e.</p> <p>Then the async one.</p> <p>```vbnet Imports System.Management.Automation.Runspaces Imports System.Management.Automation</p> <p>Namespace PowerShell Public Class RunASync Implements IRun</p> <pre><code> Private _RunSpace As Runspace Private _PipeLine As Pipeline Private WithEvents _OutPut As PipelineReader(Of PSObject) Public Event OutPutChanged(ByVal Output As String) Implements IRun.Outp= utChanged Public Sub New() _RunSpace =3D RunspaceFactory.CreateRunspace _RunSpace.Open() End Sub Public Sub Run(ByVal Command As String) Implements IRun.Run _PipeLine =3D _RunSpace.CreatePipeline(Command) _PipeLine.Input.Close() _OutPut =3D _PipeLine.Output _PipeLine.InvokeAsync() End Sub Private Sub _Output_DataReady(ByVal sender As Object, ByVal e As System= .EventArgs) Handles _OutPut.DataReady Dim data =3D _PipeLine.Output.NonBlockingRead() If data.Count &gt; 0 Then For Each d In data RaiseEvent OutPutChanged(d.ToString & Environment.NewLi= ne) Next End If If _PipeLine.Output.EndOfPipeline Then RaiseEvent RunFinished() End If End Sub Public Event RunFinished() Implements IRun.RunFinished End Class </code></pre> <p>End Namespace``` It is pretty simple, make a runspace via the factory. Make a pipeline and h= and it your command. Then close the input (very important). And Invoke the = command Async. You can then handle the dataready event from the output. Do = a NonBlockingRead from the Output and raise an event. When your are at the = end of the pipeline you can also send an event to say you are done. Easy as= pie.</p> <p>The codebehind of the form now looks like this.</p> <p>```vbnet Imports WindowsApplication2.PowerShell</p> <p>Public Class frmPowershell</p> <pre><code>Private WithEvents _Run As IRun Private _RunSync As IRun Private _RunASync As IRun Public Sub New() ' This call is required by the designer. InitializeComponent() ' Add any initialization after the InitializeComponent() call. _RunSync =3D New RunSync _RunASync =3D New RunASync End Sub Private Sub Clear_Click(ByVal sender As System.Object, ByVal e As System.Ev= entArgs) Handles btnClear.Click txtResult.Text =3D "" End Sub Private Sub Run_Click(ByVal sender As System.Object, ByVal e As System.Even= tArgs) Handles btnRun.Click Run(_RunSync) End Sub Private Sub Run(ByVal RunType As IRun) btnRun.Enabled =3D False btnRunAsync.Enabled =3D False _Run =3D RunType _Run.Run(Me.txtCommand.Text) End Sub Private Delegate Sub RunCompleted(ByVal Result As String) Private Sub _Run_OutputChanged(ByVal Output As String) Handles _Run.OutputC= hanged If Me.InvokeRequired Then Me.Invoke(New RunCompleted(AddressOf _Run_OutputChanged), New Objec= t() {Output}) Else Me.txtResult.AppendText(Output) End If End Sub Private Sub btnForLoop_Click(ByVal sender As System.Object, ByVal e As Syst= em.EventArgs) Handles btnForLoop.Click Me.txtCommand.AppendText("for($x =3D 0; $x -le 10; $x++)" & Environ= ment.NewLine) Me.txtCommand.AppendText("{" & Environment.NewLine) Me.txtCommand.AppendText("Write ""Child Task $x"" ;" & Environment.= NewLine) Me.txtCommand.AppendText("Sleep -Milliseconds 300;" & Environment.N= ewLine) Me.txtCommand.AppendText("}" & Environment.NewLine) End Sub Private Delegate Sub RunFinishedDelegate() Private Sub _Run_RunFinished() Handles _Run.RunFinished If Me.InvokeRequired Then Me.Invoke(New RunFinishedDelegate(AddressOf _Run_RunFinished), Noth= ing) Else Me.btnRun.Enabled =3D True Me.btnRunAsync.Enabled =3D True End If End Sub Private Sub btnRunAsync_Click(ByVal sender As System.Object, ByVal e As Sys= tem.EventArgs) Handles btnRunAsync.Click Run(_RunASync) End Sub </code></pre> <p>End Class``` You can now click the two buttons to notice the difference between sync and= async. Also notice the insane amount of code you have to use to make updat= ing winforms controls in an async matter (I so hate that).</p> <p>I think the next step is to create a profile variable and thus also add = an external script to our pipeline. Repeat after me, this is fun.</p> </div> <div class=3D"post-author"> =20 <div class=3D"userInfo"> <h2>About Christiaan Baes (chrissie1)</h2> =20 <img class=3D"bioPic"
